Cotton Yarn: Cotton Yarn Rises Again, Influenced by the Osaka Sampin Telegraph, While Yarn Sales Also Gradually Develop 163

The yarn market continues to be strong and bullish sentiment is rising again. This is largely due to the soaring prices of Osaka Sampin yarn, which have caused widespread anxiety. Japanese merchants are in a more bullish mood. Local merchants, due to year-end closures, mostly anticipated a slight pullback of ten yuan. Unexpectedly, news from the Japanese yarn market indicated a rising trend, which has influenced the Shanghai market.

The Further Out the Futures, the More Popular They Become

In the pre-market session for forward yarn, the one-month futures market was exceptionally quiet. Dachangcheng suddenly sold 1,000 bales, and also sold 1,000 bales for the two-month contract. When trading moved to the three-month contract, the Osaka Sampin telegraph arrived, showing a further increase of three to four yuan. Confidence was boosted, and Dachangcheng reversed course, buying over 1,000 bales in the three-month contract as a spread trade. The price surged by one and a half yuan. In the second round of trading, near-month contracts rose again, while long-term contracts remained strong. By the third closing, Sampin yarn had fallen back by 2.3 yuan. The one-month contract experienced a significant decline, but the longer-dated contracts remained firm. As a result, the one-month contract fell by one jiao compared to the previous day's close, while longer-dated contracts rose by four jiao to one yuan six jiao. In the afternoon session, trading reopened with Sampin yarn recovering its gains, and spot yarn transactions also amounted to over 900 bales. The trading floor tightened, and prices gradually rose. Consequently, all months rose again by one yuan six jiao to two yuan three to four jiao compared to the morning close. Sales included He Xing 1,550 bales, Jin Chang 900 bales, Ji Feng 850 bales, Ju Xing 750 bales, Zhen Da 650 bales, Shen Ji 1,050 bales, Da Chang Cheng 950 bales, Yi Chang 1,250 bales, Xie Cheng 800 bales, Ming De 1,850 bales, and Tai Chang 550 bales. Purchases included Yu Da 900 bales, Heng Yi 2,400 bales, Da Feng 1,950 bales, Tai Xing 2,150 bales, Geng Feng 1,500 bales, Feng Tai 700 bales, Sheng Yuan 550 bales, Chang Yu 500 bales, Yi Cheng 650 bales, and Da Chang 1,600 bales. The highest and lowest prices for the day are listed below.

Yarn Sales Weak at 1,000 Bales

Spot yarn sales are still good. A total of 963 bales were purchased by various groups throughout the day. The selling price of Japanese yarn remains strong and expensive, rising another two yuan. The purchase amounts for each group are recorded below.

Foreign Cotton Stable: Spot Cotton Buying is Booming, Arrivals are Scarcer than Before, and Actual Sales are Improving 164

The cotton market is showing signs of a turnaround daily. Arrivals from various sources are not as plentiful as before. Firstly, there is news of rising prices in the Indian and American cotton markets overseas. Secondly, the price difference between yarn and cotton is too large. Generally, those holding inventory are more optimistic about the cotton market due to the stability of foreign cotton, and the cotton market is rising.

Futures Jump Six Jiao or So

In the pre-market session for spot cotton, all months uniformly rose. Due to the large increase in Indian cotton and news of increases in American cotton, buying interest was slightly higher. Japanese merchants also came to buy. The second round of trading was unchanged. By the closing, Osaka Sampin cotton had risen by seven, eight, and nine jiao, before falling back by six or seven jiao. Yu Da also sold in large quantities, and prices fell back slightly by one jiao. As a result, all months rose by two to three jiao compared to the previous day's close. In the afternoon session, Sampin cotton rose again, and the outlook for American cotton was bullish. At the same time, Japanese factories were actively buying spot cotton, boosting confidence further. Buying momentum was strong, and market conditions progressed steadily. As a result, all months rose again by three and a half to four jiao compared to the morning close. Sales included Yu Da 7,500 dan, Yuan Da 1,400 dan, Ming Hua 1,900 dan, Yuan Yi 2,500 dan, Xie Cheng 5,300 dan, Sheng Yuan 3,000 dan, Yong Da 1,800 dan, Yi Kang 4,900 dan, Tai Xing 2,600 dan, Chang Yu 2,500 dan, Yi Chang 5,100 dan, and Fu Kang 2,400 dan. Spot cotton consumption is improving. Japanese factories are actively buying, and all transactions are in bulk. Sources include 1,100 bales of Yao cotton and 858 yuan of Tong cotton.

Osaka Telegraph, 28th: Sampin futures fell six jiao to rise two yuan seven jiao. Near-month at 262.1 yuan, long-term at 253.7 yuan. Cotton futures rose one and a half jiao to seven jiao. Recent at 71.95 yuan, long-term at 74.25 yuan.

Indian Cotton Demand Increased Last Week 166

Exports to Japan were very strong last week. Due to the strength of Japanese yarn, the demand for Indian cotton has increased. The mainland is calm. Lancashire is still actively buying new Galatz cotton, and the period is booming. Although there is a large amount of short selling in the Bombay market, it has not been affected in the slightest because exporters are continuously buying to offset old debts.

Silk Floss of Huzhou 178

— (Yan Bophoto)

The giant wheel of time has turned to the severe winter season, and everyone is preparing to rush to make winter clothes. People in Huzhou are very common to use silk floss as a wonderful product to keep out the cold, such as silk floss padded jackets and trousers; silk floss vests, silk floss robes, silk floss quilts... It is a pity that silk floss quilts, to be serviceable, must be added to and re-made every year so as not to lose their beauty and efficacy.

Every year when the oranges are green and the oranges are yellow, many old ladies put red strips on their doorsteps, specializing in making silk floss clothes for people. The daily wage is about two to half a yuan, plus board. In Suzhou, Shanghai and other places, the old women charge one, two or three yuan for remaking a silk floss robe, and the old women in Huzhou are quicker and neater. Therefore, this industry is a specialized skill, and even modern ladies who are born in Huzhou rarely do well.

Silk floss clothing is warm and light to wear, and it can also protect against bullets. If you wear silk floss padded jackets and trousers and silk floss robes at the same time, if a stray bullet comes from afar, it can indeed only penetrate into the silk floss and not touch the body. It is said that this is due to the spinning force of the bullet.

The soldiers of the Sui Army are fighting bravely and hard in the icy and snowy weather. The best thing to raise and send for rear support is silk floss vests, which have strong resistance to the cold. However, avoid padded jackets and trousers, because when padded jackets and trousers are worn, once you exercise, their heat is even stronger, and after a long time, they will eventually make you unable to move. This is because it contains the effect of clinging to power!

Camels in Peiping 179

— Haizhu

It is deep autumn. A maple leaf is like a red heart, blooming in the vast autumn fields, autumn in Peiping!

"...Unexpectedly, it is autumn again this time. Three years ago today, when you went out to see the camels in the cold wind, you were not afraid of the cold. You would run all the way to Zhengyangmen. Now the camels in Peiping have grown hair. How interesting!" Lan's letter said.

The camels have grown hair, and the autumn wind brings coldness. It is always like this in Peiping.

Since the autumn wind blew down the leaves and brought a bit of coldness, I have thought of the camels in Peiping. Although the camels in Peiping are not beautiful, their perseverance and honesty have their own loveliness. When I first arrived in Peiping, I didn't like the frost and fallen leaves in autumn, I wasn't used to listening to the bugle calls in the evening, or the train wailing in the morning mist. But I especially liked to watch the interesting camels under Zhengyangmen. At this time, such a team of camels, walking, with their long legs, moving in a staccato rhythm, their long necks, nodding bit by bit, and their high humps, swaying back and forth, paced through Zhengyangmen. The cameleers, pulling the ropes in front, were not noisy, not anxious, and accompanied the camels step by step.

It is deep autumn, and needless to say, I have a good feeling for Peiping, even the camels. The camels coming and going in the wind and sand, I have written many articles praising camels in the past three years, and have said many words of love for camels to others.

Now the autumn is getting deeper day by day, and the camels in Peiping must have grown their hair long ago. Because Peiping has those interesting camels, I am starting to express my love for them. ...On a autumn morning, stepping on the sandy ground and letting the slightly cold autumn wind blow on my body, I am also patiently counting the slow steps of the camels.

"Is it still so cold, are you still going to see the camels?" Lan often said to me with a smile. I nodded and left, and only after the sun set, in the evening in front of Zhengyangmen when it was slightly cold, would I go back alone...

The autumn is already very deep, and the camels in Peiping may have grown a lot of hair, but when can I go to Peiping?

The Beggars of Tibet 180

— Qiu Ye

To be a beggar and consider it a golden rice bowl, it can be said that this is only found in Tibet. Because in Tibet, to be a beggar, if there is no generational inheritance, it is not possible, except for the disabled. There are many Buddhist temples in Tibet, and Buddha is the most worshipped by Tibetans, so there are many people who give alms, and the income of beggars is not bad. Therefore, being a beggar is considered a golden rice bowl passed down from generation to generation, and there are many people in Tibet who rely on this for a living.

However, there is a custom that beggars cannot scold people, because people generally believe that being scolded by a beggar is unlucky. Therefore, when a beggar asks for alms, if the benefactor tells him that they have already given, he can only hang his head and leave. However, beggars have their own techniques for begging. For example, whenever they ask for alms, they try their best to flatter the benefactor or stick up their thumbs to show the benefactor's nobility. In this way, those benefactors with vanity are happy to give them some money.

Tibetan beggars are also divided into two types: Qin beggars and Skill beggars. Qin beggars ask for alms by playing a four-stringed lute and usually bring children to dance for fun. However, the tunes they play on their four-stringed lutes are all mournful and touching, so people are generally moved and give alms. As for Skill beggars, they usually carry several snakes and perform various snake tricks in front of the benefactor. Some people also bring other animals and use various skills to please the benefactor and obtain money for alms.

There are two reasons why begging in Tibet has become a hereditary profession. One is due to the training of skills and lute techniques, which are difficult for others to learn. The other is due to habit, because it is passed down from generation to generation, and the benefactors also recognize that someone is the descendant of someone, so they are happy to give alms. If you are not disabled and want to be a beggar in Tibet, you will not see a benefactor give you money all year round. With these two reasons, the descendants of beggars mostly inherit the profession of their ancestors, because it is a golden rice bowl and easier to do than other things, so why not do it? However, these beggars are all social parasites, lazy pigs who do not engage in production.

The Phoenix Returns to Its Nest 182

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter 9: Vows Made with a Cup of Water, Lantern Talks of Despair; Golden Embroidered Fingers, Red Beans Report Yearning

If he wanted something from me for himself, but our relatives have always been distant. He wouldn't suddenly have something to ask for at this time. Even if he did, it would probably be trivial matters like moving money and objects, nothing serious. He'd just go to the old lady. But he's here, and he doesn't say what he wants. He hesitates, and I can't figure out what he means. Therefore, Guoqi feels more embarrassed sitting in this room than being trapped in a besieged city. He doesn't know what to say to resolve the difficulty. Just as he's struggling, Aunt Liu brings in an express letter, asking him to stamp it. He finally has a chance to cover up his awkwardness and turns away to read the letter. Youmei smiles: "Should I leave?" Guoqi smiles: "Oh! It's nothing, just a letter from the Shanghai Bookstore urging me to submit manuscripts." Youmei sits quietly on the side, waiting for him to finish reading the letter. Then she smiles: "Cousin, since Shanghai has so many places that need you to write articles, why don't you go to Shanghai to live?" Guoqi says: "I think I still need to study a little more. Shanghai is not a place to read books." Youmei says: "Cousin, Shanghai sent an express letter urging you to submit manuscripts. They must be waiting for them. Do they want essays? Or novels?" Guoqi says: "They want both essays and novels." Youmei says: "If they send a letter, just write. Doesn't Cousin feel that the village is lacking in material?" Guoqi says: "Novels are something I imagine myself, so it's nothing. Essays need to move facts onto the paper, so sometimes I do feel it's difficult." Youmei says: "My family has many letters from the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom era. People say that if they were organized, they would make good essays. Does Cousin need that kind of material?" Guoqi says: "That's the most fashionable writing now, so how could I not need it?" Youmei smiles: "Since that's the case, I'll help Cousin. Tomorrow, I'll sort out these materials and send them to Cousin, okay?" Guoqi smiles: "That would be great. I wouldn't dare to steal someone else's credit. I'll make a note on the manuscript that the material was provided by Miss Li Youmei." Youmei smiles: "I don't care about that..." This is an unfinished sentence. Below, she should explain what she does care about. But she only says half of this sentence, smiles slightly, and ends the conversation. Guoqi fans himself with his folding fan and looks at her. She tugs at her clothes and adjusts her temples, feeling that there's nothing to explain, so she gets up to say goodbye. Her visit really gives Guoqi an indescribable feeling. Is it intentional, or unintentional? Or is there something to discuss? Or is there nothing to discuss? (116)

The Oranges of Wenzhou 184

— Bailing

Oranges are originally tropical plants, but today they are also widely grown in temperate zones. They are afraid of the cold winter, so gardeners cover them with dog manure and river mud - but pig manure will kill them, and they are prone to pests. Covering them with sulfur powder will prevent this.

The orange tree is an evergreen shrub, and it is lovely even in winter. Therefore, Zhang Jiuling wrote in his poem: "In Jiangnan, there are red oranges, evergreen forests throughout the winter. Is it because the climate is warm, or does it have a steadfast heart in the cold winter?" The trunk is one or two zhang tall, with small thorns on the stems. The leaves are pinnate, and the petioles have wing-like leaflets. In early summer, it blooms with small white flowers with five petals. In early winter, the fruits ripen, flattened and round, yellow or red in color, with thin skin that is easy to peel, and a slightly sweet and sour taste. Tang Lu Guimeng has a poem praising it, saying: "Fine jade has juice, must yield in taste, bright pearls are unique, also ashamed of roundness," the words are accurate.

At the beginning of winter, the oranges are ripe, with round fruits and red color, which contrast with the green branches and leaves, making them most lovely. Ming Qian Sheng once wrote: "Dense golden balls can't help but be stolen, most pity them hanging on the treetops. The old man's mouth and stomach have no share, leaving them for the eyes in late autumn." He can be said to be a good connoisseur.

However, the function of oranges is not in appreciation, but in providing food. Silver plate red fruits, the flavor is both rich and the sweet pulp and juice are especially good for digestion. The best ones are used to entertain guests, and the inferior ones are made into orange cakes. The brine can be used to make wine, spices, or fruit syrup. The skin and pulp can be used in medicine, with nothing wasted.

Guangdong, Fuzhou, and Wenzhou in our country are all famous for producing oranges, and I know more about Wenzhou oranges. According to the Qunfang Pu, oranges come from Taizhou, Suzhou, west from Jingzhou, south from Min and Guang Fuzhou, but none are better than Wenzhou. It can be said to be highly praised.

The migration of the orange production area in Wenzhou is recorded in Lao Da's Oujiang Yizhi: "The soil of Yongjia is suitable for planting oranges. Han Shouyan Zhi's records can prove this. In the Song Dynasty, they were produced in Xishan, and Ye Zhengze's poem 'There are forests of orange trees' is also true. Later, they flourished in Hetian of Taoshan, then Shanggang, then Nan Xianyang, and gradually to Wutian. The migration of the earth's qi is from northwest to southeast."

There are many varieties of Wenzhou oranges. Han Yanzhi's Orange Record says: "Produced in Wenzhou, there are fourteen varieties: Huangju (Yellow Orange), Taju (Collapsed Orange), Baoju (Bag Orange), Mianju (Cotton Orange), Shaju (Sand Orange), Lizhiju (Lychee Orange), Ruan Tiaoyaju (Soft Branch Bud Orange), Youju (Oil Orange), Luju (Green Orange), Jinju (Golden Orange), Ruju (Milk Orange), Ziranju (Natural Orange), Zao Huangju (Early Yellow Orange), Dongju (Frozen Orange)." According to the Tongzhi: "The oranges of Dongjia are similar to those of Zhejiang West. Their taste is sweet and delicious, and those without seeds are the best. The Ruju mentioned in the Guangyu Ji is this."

Han Yanzhi was a Song Dynasty person who knew Wenzhou and wrote the Orange Record in three volumes. The upper volume describes citrus products, one orange product, the middle volume describes eighteen orange products, and the lower volume describes planting methods. I have not seen the Orange Record, so I know it but not in detail, but I learned from a friend: "The best oranges are of three kinds: first, Wenzhou is the honey orange, which is the best variety, large and slightly flat, the outer skin is dark red, yellow, the skin is easily separated from the pulp, the segments are about ten, fragrant, sweet and delicious, ripening at the end of October, and can be stored for a long time. The second is the red honey orange, the fruit is round and flat, with only traces of the navel, slightly concave around, and the pedicel is raised. The peel is smooth and yellowish-red. The third is the bag orange, the fruit is small, flattened and round, with a raised pedicel and a slightly low and flat fruit pit. The outer skin is yellow, and there are about six to ten segments. It is produced in Dongting, Jiangsu Province, hence it is also known as Dongting Red.

In the past, Ye Shi had a poem about orange branches: "Honey orange segments have a golden skin, short days hang sparsely in people's homes. Judgmental frost cuts through the dew to load the boat, not singing Yangzhi, but singing orange branches." From this, we can know the prosperity of the orange industry in Wenzhou. All guests who come to Wenzhou must first taste honey oranges for pleasure.

The Snakes of Guangdong 185

— Nangong Sheng

Snakes are poisonous animals. Although some are not poisonous, there are more poisonous ones, such as the Red-banded krait, the Banded krait, and the Grey snake, all of which are highly venomous. Only a few kinds like the green snake are non-poisonous. Generally speaking, poisonous snakes have triangular heads, while non-poisonous snakes have flat, round heads.

There are the most poisonous snakes in tropical regions, and there are very strange poisonous snakes. For example, India produces two-headed snakes and human-faced snakes, whose venom is unparalleled. A few years ago, these two kinds of strange snakes were displayed in the Shanghai Great World. According to the snake owner, an Indian, 300,000 Indians die from these two kinds of snake venom every year in India. This is such an amazing number!

The largest snakes are pythons, which can be twenty or thirty zhang long and as thick as round barrels. They are produced in large quantities in Africa, Annam, and other places. The natives regard pythons as delicious food. After catching them, they are cooked and used to entertain guests. This is because the snake's venom is all in the head. As long as the head is discarded, there is no venom, and it is a very delicious food.

Guangdong Province in our country is a place where snakes are considered a delicacy. In recent years, it has gradually become popular in Shanghai. In winter, Guangdong restaurants in Shanghai use eating snakes as a selling point. Besides people from Guangdong and Guangxi, there are quite a few people who like to eat snakes. Therefore, the trend of eating snakes has gradually become widespread. According to Guangdong people who are good at eating snakes, snake meat is not only delicious, but also has the effect of dispelling wind, cold, promoting blood circulation, strengthening the body, and treating skin diseases. Therefore, it is a must-eat every winter. The number of snakes eaten every year is considerable.

Guangdong people are very particular about eating snakes. There are two kinds of snakes that they eat: one is a large snake, which is called the Golden Leopard because it has money-like spots on its body. The large ones weigh seventy or eighty catties. We often see the sign "Today we will butcher a Golden Leopard" at the entrance of Guangdong restaurants. The other is a small snake, which must be cooked with three kinds of snakes, called Three-Snake Stew. However, the effect is not as great as that of the Golden Leopard.

Snake meat has three names. When cooked with chicken, it is called the "Dragon and Phoenix Meeting." When cooked with civet cat, it is called the "Dragon and Tiger Meeting." There is also a kind that is pure snake meat, called the "Three-Snake Stew."

Snake bones are poisonous, so after killing the snake, the bones must be removed completely. Otherwise, the poison will be passed on to the people who eat the snake. It is said that the death of Zhu Zhaoxin, a negotiator between Guangdong and Guangxi in the past, was due to eating snake bones. Snake bile is also regarded as a precious thing, because it has the effect of improving eyesight and dispelling wind and dampness. The best is the "Cinnabar Bile," which comes with a cinnabar bag. Usually, snake bile is eaten by drinking snake bile wine, which is made by dripping bile juice into undiluted sorghum wine. One drop of bile juice in one cup of undiluted sorghum wine turns the wine green, which is beneficial to the human body. However, it is very difficult to extract the bile. If you are not careful, it will break. This all depends on the skill of the snake killer. In Guangzhou, famous snake-killing chefs become the center of attention in winter, because wealthy families have to eat snakes and have to ask him to kill them. The price they get each month is often around several hundred yuan. The way Guangdong people eat snakes can be imagined.

In Guangzhou, there is also a trend of eating snake bile exclusively. Seven or eight people gather and go to the snake shops outside the city that specialize in selling snake bile to eat snake bile in a big way. This kind of snake is a small snake, and the snake bile is very small. Each person has to eat five or six, and seven or eight people need thirty or forty snake lives. Moreover, they want the most alive and most agile snakes. The people who extract the snake bile have developed the skill to know where the snake bile is. They use their hands to dig out the entire bile from the live snake. Isn't this too cruel!

Shen Bao Medical Supplement

Seeking Medicine vs. Seeking Medical Care 186

— Fan Shouyuan

Chinese people have a very bad habit when it comes to dealing with illnesses, which is that when they have a problem, they only want to seek medicine and are unwilling to seek medical care. This kind of behavior of seeking medicine and not seeking medical care has harmed the bodies of many patients and lost the lives of many people!

In their minds, they think that going to consult a doctor when they are sick is only to ask the doctor to prescribe a prescription and get some medicine to take. If there is a simple way to skip the step of consulting a doctor and directly get the medicine, wouldn't that be the same as achieving the goal? The purpose of taking medicine can also be achieved in the same way, but it saves two extra steps: it can save the doctor's time for examination and also save a consultation fee when consulting a doctor. Isn't this a win-win situation?

With this kind of mentality of being afraid of trouble, saving procedures, being greedy for petty gains, and taking shortcuts, once they have a problem, they are unwilling to go to a doctor properly, but instead find medicine to take randomly. So, for headaches, they take "aspirin," headache medicine; for stomachaches, they take morphine, stomachache powder; by extension, for mental weakness, they take brain tonics, and for blood deficiency, they take blood tonics. They don't know that a headache is just a symptom of a disease, not the disease itself; there are various complex reasons for headaches, and aspirin alone cannot solve all headaches. Of course, there are headaches that are cured by taking aspirin, but there are also headaches that are made worse by taking aspirin. Stomachaches are also just a common symptom of many things. Morphine can temporarily stop a stomachache, but it may not cure all the diseases that cause stomachaches! Also, mental weakness is a self-reported symptom by the patient. Is it really mental weakness? That is still a question. Blood deficiency is also the patient's own imagination. Is it really blood deficiency? That cannot be determined either. Moreover, what is the root cause of mental weakness? What is the cause of blood deficiency? If you don't first understand the root cause of mental weakness and blood deficiency and then take medicine randomly, how can you expect the medicine to cure the disease? But understanding the reasons for mental weakness, blood deficiency, headaches, and stomachaches requires a doctor's examination.

The patient's desire in seeking medical care seems to be only to take medicine, and the purpose of taking medicine is of course to cure the disease. But you must know that without first seeking medical diagnosis, you cannot understand the root cause of the problem. Without understanding the details of the illness and taking medicine randomly, not only will there be no guarantee of curing the disease, but it will often lead to accidents, messes, and endanger life!

Curing the disease is of course the doctor's responsibility, but identifying the disease is even more the doctor's skill. Taking medicine is a tool for curing the disease, but sometimes there are many other methods for curing the disease besides taking medicine. If you encounter diseases that do not require taking medicine to cure, and you take medicine randomly, wouldn't you be harming yourself instead of benefiting? Whether to use medicine to cure the disease or use other methods to treat the disease can only be decided by a doctor who can identify the disease in order to avoid this kind of unexpected harm! Only then can you achieve the effect of the medicine curing the disease!

Prospects for Medical and Health Undertakings in the 26th Year 187

— Guo Ziliang

The New Year of the 26th year is just a few days away! We are pleased that our public health guide, the "Medical and Pharmaceutical Special Issue," will add a glorious year to its history amidst the gratitude and anticipation of the masses. However, we cannot be satisfied with this or consider this the end goal. As each year passes, the responsibilities we bear increase rather than decrease. At the same time, the public's expectations for this publication, as seen in their words, show a desire for increased contributions from this publication, with particularly high expectations. Similarly, other medical and pharmaceutical facilities and health initiatives naturally increase their effectiveness and achievements with each passing year. This pattern repeats itself year after year, but why is it being mentioned specifically this year? It is because the rapid development of health undertakings, the opening and expansion of health defenses, especially in the past year or two, including this year, have yielded unexpectedly significant results. Taking the facts before us, the successful preparation for the National Health Education Annual Conference, the Nanchang Leprosy Hospital, and the Zhongzheng Medical College have all been established or are in progress this year. There are many other achievements as well, so the backbone of medical and health undertakings this year has become increasingly solid. At the same time, the era of medical and health undertakings transforming from embryonic to formed is upon us.

At this eve of the upcoming 26th year, at this moment of transition between old and new endeavors, at the beginning of the medical community's two-year work cycle, how can we not reflect on our past mistakes and formulate future directions? Moreover, the solidity of the foundation is a prediction of the success or failure of our profession. The success or failure of our undertakings and the interests of the nation are naturally closely linked. Therefore, medical and health undertakings in the 26th year, under the aforementioned circumstances, occupy a crucial position where success or failure hinges on this single move. Now, with utmost sincerity, I wish all medical and pharmaceutical personnel to thoroughly reform our work with twelvefold effort, sweep away all obstacles in our path, and shoulder the great mission of maintaining the life of our entire nation and enriching the strength of the nation and people. I also hope for the following:

(1) Unify the System and Rectify the Internal Structure: Strengthen internal organization and unite various health agencies so that they can operate under the same governing body, pursuing agreed-upon policies with collaborative goals. Our country lacks the aforementioned unity. There are even unqualified individuals filling positions in health administration, performing duties beyond their capabilities, which often leads to inefficiency. Sometimes the division of powers is unclear, and directives from higher authorities are not implemented on time, or are even overtly disobeyed. These are all manifestations of an unsound internal organization, which affects the progress of the entire undertaking. As for the various health agencies, such as those run by the national government, provincial governments, county governments, and private organizations, they maintain extremely defined boundaries and lack a unified system due to limited authority. Each fulfills its own duties, taking a wait-and-see attitude, which greatly hinders the progress of health undertakings. Therefore, all national health agencies should abandon the above concepts and take mutual assistance, research, advocacy, and obedience to the instructions of any senior health agency as their duty. At the same time, the government should control all health agencies, especially in this era of national crisis, and strive to avoid a scattered mindset and organization.

(2) Organize Aviation Rescue: In today's rapidly changing world situation, with the East Asian crisis imminent, we can no longer afford to wait and see. Rescue work is a major task in wartime. However, human rescue is time-consuming and laborious, and often fails to achieve the purpose of rescue. For example, fierce battles at the front may last for months, and the number of wounded in those months cannot be accommodated by the temporary hospitals or the few existing hospitals at the front. If they are transferred to the rear, transportation will inevitably be congested during wartime, or there may be no means of transportation in remote areas. Under such circumstances, the lives of the wounded on the battlefield are in grave danger and cannot withstand repeated transfers. Even if the front hospitals can accommodate them, the lightly wounded may be saved, but the seriously wounded in the battlefield may not receive the meticulous and dedicated care of the doctors. If we put ourselves in the position of the wounded at that time, although many are difficult to save, those who can be saved are also difficult to survive. Therefore, to achieve rapid and effective rescue, we must utilize the power of aircraft. Amidst the call for aviation to save the nation, our national medical and pharmaceutical community should vigorously promote the work of donating funds to purchase rescue aircraft. The government should also pay attention to the lives of the wounded in wartime, quickly add equipment within its means, and organize the training of aviation rescue personnel. Alternatively, it could take advantage of the opportunity of transport planes returning empty from the front to accommodate some of the wounded and transport them to the rear. In the future, if several rescue work teams can be realized, not only will the effectiveness be enormous, but the number of rescued wounded who can regain their lives will be dozens of times greater than the work of several hospitals and rescue personnel at the front!

(3) Correct the Distorted Development of Medical and Health Undertakings: If one examines the country with a discerning eye, the following conclusion can be drawn: In major cities, medical and health undertakings such as hospitals, clinics, health centers, and epidemic prevention stations are so complete and developed that anyone can enjoy health and treatment, and the opportunities are gradually increasing. However, if you shift your gaze to other places, it is not the same. In many neglected counties within relatively developed provinces, one can still see scattered clinics, one or two incomplete and religious hospitals, or many unqualified doctors residing there, engaging in business. When someone seeks treatment, they are seen as a rare commodity, and exorbitant prices are charged. As a result, the poor never dare to inquire. In the end, such situations are truly countless. Other remote counties in border provinces simply do not have even a shadow of these things, let alone any health undertakings. Perhaps there are exceptions, but they are very rare! As for the villages attached to the cities, they enjoy favorable treatment. For example, Zhenjiang, as the provincial capital of Jiangsu Province, and the villages under the jurisdiction of Zhenjiang County, are therefore unexpectedly fortunate. Almost all the seven districts in the countryside have three or four provincial-run health experiment zones, and each district has a district health center, as well as health stations, maternity hospitals, clinics, and so on. Moreover, the agencies and scales contained in the health experiment sites are very large. Although this distorted development is due to the needs of dense urban populations, we must also pay attention to places outside of cities, so that all parts of the country, whether remote villages or secluded counties, can receive the baptism of non-profit new medicine and achieve the simultaneous and balanced development of medical and health undertakings in various places.

(4) Correct Nurses' Mentality and Restrict Unqualified Personnel from Parasitizing the New Medical Field: Nursing ethics have always been emphasized by the medical communities of all countries in the world, and their importance is self-evident. However, the general impression of hospitals in our country is unsatisfactory. This cannot be said to be due to inadequate training, but it is entirely a psychological effect. Look at the nurses in the first and second class wards of each hospital. They treat patients with great courtesy and are very serious in their care and all other work. But in the ordinary wards or people's hospitals, it is completely different. They frown and show a look of disgust towards the patients. If a patient asks a question, they scold them as if they are a nuisance. There are many, many such facts, or even worse. Therefore, the impact on the patient is great, and the reputation of the medical community also suffers considerable losses. Generally, people retain a fondness for the rich and a dislike for the poor from a young age, and this psychology is not easily changed. Therefore, when serving in society, it manifests itself at all times and in all places. I believe that this situation is particularly shameful when it occurs in the medical field. To reform this bad phenomenon, we must fundamentally treat it, that is, we must find ways to correct the psychology during the initial nurse training period. As for unqualified personnel parasitizing the medical field, they are everywhere, especially those heinous quacks. They rely entirely on their glib tongues to solicit customers, talking eloquently and engaging in deceptive monetary practices. If they perform surgery on the sick, it is even more dangerous. Speaking of the mixing of unqualified personnel, it is also very annoying, because they often make many unexpected mistakes, and thus the reputation of the new medical community often suffers unexpected blows from them. Therefore, in the future, we will not only eliminate quacks, but also restrict unqualified medical personnel who directly affect our reputation.

Page 16

(5) Seek to Expand the Sources of Funding for Medical and Health Undertakings: To expand medical and health undertakings, there must be great economic strength. However, our country has a limited economic capacity. Therefore, to expand medical and health undertakings, we must seek other methods. Moreover, our country's understanding of new medical and health undertakings is very simple. As for private donations to establish medical undertakings, they are also limited. Therefore, the government should also add appropriate edification to public education to make the people of the whole country know its importance, know that it cannot be lacking. At the same time, local health authorities must also find ways to publicize the great righteousness, so that the people can voluntarily donate money that is wasted on useless things, such as superstitious consumption of tobacco and alcohol, and designate certain local banks or agency stores to collect donations on a regular basis so that people can donate at any time. If this can be done, there will definitely be good results in donations every year and everywhere. If this is used to expand health and medical undertakings, the value obtained will be immeasurable.

Prevention of Infant Colds and Attention in the Home 188

— Medical Doctor Gotoshima Hiroshi, Translated by Li Shouzhen

In the blink of an eye, December has arrived and winter is here once more. At this time of year, colds are common and widespread. Families with beloved children, especially during this busy time of year and the approach of the happy new year, must be particularly attentive to the evil winds, which are the source of all illnesses, and not neglect them even for a moment. Therefore, we have invited Mr. Gotoshima (Vice-Director of the Mitsuwa Enjudo Hospital), from the perspective of a pediatrician, to give instructions as a reference for the home.

As the weather grows colder day by day, diseases of the respiratory system are increasing, especially the common cold. It is most often spread from adults to children, and from one person to the whole family, like a family infection. Fortunately, serious cases are rare. After contracting the illness, the fever is initially around 39 degrees Celsius, and many people cannot sleep well at night because of the cough. When this becomes severe, it becomes catarrhal pneumonia: the fever lasts from one week to two weeks. In the case of an epidemic, it goes without saying that absolute prevention is very difficult, but it is very important to pay attention at home for mild cases. That said, it is of course necessary to seek medical attention promptly if a child who is usually healthy contracts the illness, but it is absolutely unacceptable to assume that the child is healthy and pay no attention to it. It is not uncommon for children to go to school casually with a cough, only to become overwhelmed when the illness worsens. Therefore, even with mild cold symptoms, even if the child is very strong, it is important to make sure that he or she does not go out for a few days, and it is best to postpone bathing, etc. It is common to have a slight sore throat, a fever that lasts for a week, and an inability to sleep at night. In this way, nephritis can also occur. It is not uncommon for the strongest children to shout, "It's cold, it's cold," when their faces are already swollen, which is a clear sign of nephritis. Two brothers have both contracted it, and it is not uncommon for the disease to become incurable due to lack of attention. In this way, even if the child is weak, if you pay attention to him or her, even if he or she contracts an illness, he or she will recover quickly. (To be continued)

A Discussion on the Three-Character Noun "Tropical Diseases" (Part 2) 189

— A Soldier

One is the necessity of understanding so-called tropical diseases, because many of these diseases also have traces in our country, which is located in temperate and humid zones. One is that they should be classified and selectively incorporated into the textbooks of various disciplines. The reason is that, first, the name is correct and the language is smooth, and second, it is easy to enable medical students to obtain a universal infusion of knowledge about these diseases during their studies. To be fair, in so-called tropical medicine, there are also many purely tropical products or endemic diseases that are not easily seen in our territory, and there is no need to know them. Following the above second point of view can save medical students time and concepts, which seems to fit the so-called "killing two birds with one stone." Starting with the name "tropical disease" and establishing another name during the study period will cause medical students to have a distant discrimination, which will lose the original intention of attaching importance to it. I would like to ask the experts, is this not also a foolish idea? Summarizing the above, it can be briefly said that:

(1) The so-called tropical disease is a term defined by Europe and the United States based on geographical location.

(2) Most of the so-called tropical diseases also exist in temperate and cold zones.

(3) The main diseases in tropical diseases are endemic or epidemic infectious diseases caused by bacteria and parasitic organisms, and the clinical field is the widest in internal medicine, followed by dermatology and venereal surgery.

(4) Most of the diseases in tropical diseases are our endemic diseases, and we need to understand them.

(5) Most of the old textbooks did not include the above diseases. The Ministry of Health and the Ministry of Education, in view of the necessity of understanding this subject, have resolved to include tropical diseases as a compulsory subject in the later period of medical studies.

(6) Personal observation believes that from our geographical standpoint and from the needs of reality, we may as well take the essence and discard the dross, select the common diseases in our country, classify them and incorporate them into the textbooks of various disciplines, and there is no need to establish another name. This will enable medical students to obtain the necessary knowledge and the concept of equal importance with other disciplines in the original program imperceptibly.

Of course, we also hope that one day our medical students will have the motivation to specialize in tropical medicine. The Ministry of Health is already holding tropical medicine training courses, but it is only for the research and prevention of scattered endemic infectious diseases in various places! I am young and have little knowledge. The above is only based on my personal experiences, and there may be errors and inaccuracies. Moreover, education is a matter for the country, and the state has established officials who have special duties. There is no need for a young boy to chatter. However, I do not want to remain silent, so I offer my foolishness as material for the wise authorities to consult extensively. The words of a madman may be explored by a sage. I only have such an idea! (End)

Common Sense of Hygiene for Diseases of the Eyes, Ears, Nose, and Throat 190

— Tang Renjin

(113) General Symptoms of Throat Diseases

General symptoms of throat diseases. There are four main ones. They are (1) sore throat and pain when swallowing, (2) speech disorders, (3) breathing disorders, and (4) abnormal sensations. These four obvious symptoms often occur in any type of throat disease. A detailed description is given below.

(1) Sore Throat and Pain when Swallowing - Often an inevitable symptom in acute inflammation of the throat (such as tonsillitis, peritonsillar abscess, and phlegmon), chronic infiltration, and ulcers (such as tuberculous ulcers and cancer). The pain is not only felt when swallowing food, but also when swallowing saliva. Therefore, the patient's face often shows a painful expression. The head is often tilted to the affected side. The pain sometimes radiates to the ear on the affected side, or to the back of the head, temporal region, and mastoid process. There may be pain.

(2) Speech Disorders - When the mucous membrane of the posterior wall, lateral wall, and oral isthmus of the throat is swollen and enlarged, the shape of the throat cavity changes. The contraction of the muscles is also incomplete. The sound becomes distorted. The pronunciation of palatal sounds becomes difficult or even impossible. This type of sound is called an occlusive sound or a constricted sound. It is generally seen in tonsillitis, peritonsillar abscess, and retropharyngeal abscess. When the palate is perforated, ruptured, or the palatal veil is infiltrated and paralyzed, the closure between the oral cavity and the nasopharyngeal cavity is often incomplete. At this time, most of the exhaled air escapes into the nasal cavity. The sound produced by this situation is specifically called open nasal speech. Also, if the palatal veil is adhered to the posterior wall of the pharynx, or a tumor occurs in the throat cavity, most or all of the nasopharyngeal cavity is blocked. The sound produced by this situation is specifically called closed nasal speech.

(3) Breathing Disorders - Mostly caused by abscesses, tumors, infiltration, and foreign objects, resulting in the blockage of the nasopharyngeal cavity and causing disorders of nasal breathing. Since nasal breathing is obstructed, one must rely solely on oral breathing. Repeated snoring, sleep disorders, and other symptoms occur.

(4) Abnormal Sensations - One of the symptoms that patients often complain about in throat diseases is abnormal sensations. The most common sensations include itching, burning, dryness, and a foreign body sensation, etc. The irritation from abnormal sensations can repeatedly trigger coughing.

(114) Pharyngitis

Pharyngitis is inherently of two types: acute and chronic. However, based on case evidence, most cases are chronic. Therefore, I will now briefly discuss only the chronic type.

The most obvious cause of chronic pharyngitis is persistent oral breathing. Other causes include changes in climate (such as dry air and rapid changes in temperature), inhalation of dust, toxic gases and vapors, and abuse of alcoholic beverages and tobacco. In addition, there is a genetic relationship. Furthermore, diseases of the nose and paranasal sinuses, chronic tonsillitis, abnormal constitution (anemia and chlorosis), and chronic congestion of the upper respiratory tract (polycythemia, constipation, and heart, kidney, and lung diseases, etc.) are also common causes of this disease.

The disease types of chronic pharyngitis can be divided into three categories based on the differences in pathological anatomy and the localized area of inflammation, as follows:

I. Classification based on differences in pathological anatomy:

(1) Chronic Hypertrophic Pharyngitis

(2) Granular Pharyngitis

(3) Atrophic Pharyngitis

II. Classification based on the localized area of inflammation:

(1) Diffuse Pharyngitis

(2) Nasopharyngeal Catarrh

(3) Lateral Pharyngeal Band Inflammation

A detailed description of each of the above categories will not be provided.

The most common subjective symptoms of chronic pharyngitis are abnormal secretions and hyperesthesia. In the morning, a large amount of mucus is often coughed up by coughing. In addition, there are neck tension, a foreign body sensation in the throat, itching, dryness, ear pain when swallowing (lateral pharyngeal band inflammation), voice and speech disorders, and fatigue.

The treatment for chronic pharyngitis is to strictly prohibit irritation from tobacco and alcohol, pay attention to changes in climate, treat diseases of the nose and paranasal sinuses, chronic tonsillitis, abnormal constitution, and chronic congestion of the upper respiratory tract. As for local treatment, it must be carried out under the direction of a doctor.
